> 
> Ignored

Each strategy trade function (Trade_X) got this line:  
result &= signal_method <= 0 || Convert::ValueToOp(curr_trend) == cmd;  
so when X_SignalMethod is 0 or positive, it only trades with the current trend. Otherwise, when negative, it trades all the time. The easiest would be to run optimization and find the better TrendMethod which works for the current months, as EA was optimized using older years (and the market is always changing). If you'd like to compile v1.072 (tag), you need to clone the main repo recursively and find the right HEAD for class repo. For example, if you go to [GitHub](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/tree/v1.072/src/include/EA) and you click on [public-classes @ 93f39c2](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/tree/93f39c2ce97364df221d981c4a4cba5d7e0504f6) folder, this is the version (93f39c2) of EA31337-classes files to use. Using git, you just checkout to that version (git checkout -f v1.072) and you should have the right files. But I don't think backporting will help, it could be not a simple change, but you can try. I think the easiest is to optimize the params one by one (starting from TrendMethod), or per group of params, so they can work better. Or find signal method values which can work despite the trend changes.  
  

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11050285#post11050285 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> One of my accounts is currently sitting in 40% drawdown so I wonder if that is considered normal? It has reached the limit of open orders, so cannot trade more. This is the 6k account I mentioned before which is approx 10k now (in balance).
> 
> Ignored

Unfortunately, losses play some role as well. So from 6k, you get 10k within 2-3 weeks with a bit of luck due to joining at the right time and trading along with the trend, only to prepare for the switch (or bad market conditions), so you can afford the losses which comes to the trend change. The risk is that the EA doesn't know whether the trend changed (nobody knows) as it also could be a false-positive. So by trial and error, the losses needs to be taken into the account, in order to adjust to the new market conditions. In the ideal scenario, you want to earn 2-3x more, then afford to lose less when the market goes bad. Successful trading comes with the right trend detection logic working well, otherwise trading lower timeframes against the main trend could be a suicide. Normally EA should detect the losses and take into the account, and lower the lot size to the minimum when the market conditions are bad (based on the profit factor per strategy), but it can take some time to adjust.

> Ignored

I wasn't expecting 70% in the first 3 weeks on the forward testing, that sounds very promising, so thanks for testing. Even with the loses, this still shows a great hidden potential. I hope it's going to continuing like that. I was mainly focusing on the backtests which didn't perform so well and they looked very unstable and didn't know exactly how to approach the problem due to limitations. As far as I remember, v1.072 was heavily optimized (update below), but my understanding is, the latest version of EA has been optimized only to its ~20-30% full potential and also needs some heavy optimization work, that's the reason most of the strategies were disabled by default. This month I can introduce to the method of backtesting using _Docker_ in order to attempt the optimization of the latest version.  
  
Here are the optimization results which were used for the EA, so it can give a brief idea how complex it is:  
\- [v1.072 part 1](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/pull/317/files) (combined results from 1084 commits) + [v1.072 part 2](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/pull/319/files) (combined results from 2281 commits)  
Assuming each commit approximately is one optimization (~few hours run each) or backtest run (~1h), it took over 3365 tests (the number could be doubled as not all were accepted to be merged, failed or needed to be re-run) to find the right parameters for it. Let's assume each run is around 1h (in reality, some runs took days in a row), it makes over 140 days which is like running optimization tests constantly for over 4.5 months in a row (24h/7).  
And here are the results for next versions:  
\- [v1.073 RC1](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/pull/320/files) (1508 commits/tests)  
\- [v1.074](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/pull/321/files) (327 commits/tests)  
\- v1.075 got only fixes and some manual optimization runs, no further optimizations are done yet.

  * [#187](/thread/post/11053423#post11053423 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:30am  May 13, 2018 2:06am | Edited 2:30am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11052971#post11052971 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I looked in the commits for the optimization of v1.074 and CloseOrderAfterXHours is now set to 24 hours rather than 72 hours like in the set for v1.072. I am going to try that for the next weeks of forward testing.
> 
> Ignored

The _CloseOrderAfterXHours_ is a very speculative param. On one side, during trading you want to keep your order as long as it's necessary till you hit your stops (e.g., just in case the order gets better, or you get attached to it), on the other hand, during backtesting, you don't want to keep your orders too long to avoid few lucky trades poisoning your overall results.  
  
In general, the [optimization results for v1.073](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/blob/67b9680288fed9a145d7eccabfb5cc20608a9f18/EURUSD/default/10000USD/20-spread/5-digits/2014-2016/_optimization_results/All-CloseOrderAfterXHours--EURUSD-10000USD-2014-2016year-20spread-DS-test.txt) shows, the longer you wait, the better.  
Period 30 Minutes (M30) 2014.01.06 00:00 - 2016.12.30 21:30 (2014.01.01 - 2016.12.31)  
Model Control points (a very crude method)  
Initial deposit 10000.00; Spread 20  
Pass Profit Total trades Profit factor Expected Payoff Drawdown $ Drawdown %  
1 5963.88 4302 1.04 1.39 12027.22 72.10 CloseOrderAfterXHours=0;  
4 4548.52 5783 1.03 0.79 9646.13 65.65 CloseOrderAfterXHours=72;  
6 3970.98 5695 1.03 0.70 7842.83 51.07 CloseOrderAfterXHours=120;  
3 3285.71 6511 1.02 0.50 10278.19 66.28 CloseOrderAfterXHours=48;  
2 1001.18 8141 1.01 0.12 9911.01 70.30 CloseOrderAfterXHours=24;  
5 314.52 6091 1.00 0.05 10293.47 71.50 CloseOrderAfterXHours=96;  
  
And [another one for 2016](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/blob/67b9680288fed9a145d7eccabfb5cc20608a9f18/EURUSD/default/10000USD/20-spread/5-digits/2016/_optimization_results/All-CloseOrderAfterXHours--EURUSD-10000USD-2016year-20spread-DS-test.txt) (missing other values probably means they failed to provide positive profit):  
Period 30 Minutes (M30) 2016.01.06 03:00 - 2016.12.30 21:30 (2016.01.01 - 2016.12.31)  
Pass Profit Total trades Profit factor Expected Payoff Drawdown $ Drawdown %  
1 17370.37 1727 1.27 10.06 8451.76 44.77 CloseOrderAfterXHours=96;  
  
So for the forward trading, I think it's probably better to keep it 72h or 0 (for none), for optimization tests, to find the best technical params, it's better to keep it tight (like 24h) as the technical indicator conditions which were used to open the trade are no longer relevant the next day as support, resistance and pivot points changes, so the profit results from the next day should be not considered. On the other side, when you optimized params using 24h closure, you don't know whether you will improve or worse things when you change it during forward trading, because the change will alter the logic which hasn't been tested.  
  
Here is another [optimization results for v1.074](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Lite-Sets/blob/59cac57bcce1efef5f389a0bfb7ef8311c8853a2/EURUSD/default/10000USD/20-spread/5-digits/2014-2016/_optimization_results/All-CloseOrderAfterXHours--EURUSD-10000USD-2014-2016year-20spread-DS-test.txt):  
  
Period 30 Minutes (M30) 2014.01.06 00:00 - 2016.12.30 21:30 (2014.01.01 - 2016.12.31)  
Model Every tick (the most precise method based on all available least timeframes)  
Initial deposit 10000.00; Spread 20  
Pass Profit Total trades Profit factor Expected Payoff Drawdown $ Drawdown %  
1 1283.37 779 1.28 1.65 502.41 4.85 CloseOrderAfterXHours=0;  
6 1154.21 779 1.25 1.48 502.41 4.80 CloseOrderAfterXHours=120;  
5 1117.84 779 1.24 1.43 502.41 4.91 CloseOrderAfterXHours=96;  
4 881.71 499 1.26 1.77 396.87 3.75 CloseOrderAfterXHours=72;  
2 -54.77 221 0.95 -0.25 338.19 3.36 CloseOrderAfterXHours=24;  
3 -54.77 221 0.95 -0.25 338.19 3.36 CloseOrderAfterXHours=48;  
  
So what's the best value for it? I don't know. But it's good to find out on the forward testing.

  * [#195](/thread/post/11060574#post11060574 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:42pm  May 15, 2018 8:11pm | Edited 8:42pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11059783#post11059783 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> For CCI, is there a maximum value for the signal method? It just says "0-" with no maximum in the inputs. I looked through the source and couldn't find the information.
> 
> Ignored

CCI was added in the recent version. The range for the signal method is between 0-63 as per the following code (in [Trade_CCI()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/blob/v1.075/src/EA31337.mq4#L2071)):  
if ((signal_method % 1) == 0) result &= cci[period][CURR] > cci[period][PREV]; # 1  
if ((signal_method % 2) == 0) result &= cci[period][PREV] > cci[period][FAR]; # 2  
if ((signal_method % 4) == 0) result &= cci[period][PREV] < -signal_level; # 3  
if ((signal_method % 8) == 0) result &= cci[period][FAR] < -signal_level; # 4  
if ((signal_method % 16) == 0) result &= cci[period][CURR] - cci[period][PREV] > cci[period][PREV] - cci[period][FAR]; # 5  
if ((signal_method % 32) == 0) result &= cci[period][FAR] > 0; # 6  
The conditions are implemented [bitwisely](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitwise_operation#AND) (logical AND operation). For example, CCI has 6 main 'if' conditions, so by checking 0-64 range, you can basically test all the permutations. So 0 (for CCI*_SignalMethod) means no filter signal conditions (that is every trade will be executed; high volume trading), '1' value means execute only when 1st condition is matched (CURR>PREV - current CCI value is higher than from the previous bar for buy, opposite for the sell), '2' - execute only on 2nd condition, '3' (1+2) - execute on both 1st and 2nd conditions, '4' - only on 4th conditions, '5' (1+4) only on 1st and 4th, '6' (2+4), '7' (1+2+4), '8', '9' (1+8) and so on, and '63' means all 6 conditions needs to be matched to execute the trades. This is very powerful, as you can test all the combinations for each timeframe and set the unique conditions for each strategy and each timeframe which works for the given market conditions (pair). In the later versions, new conditions can be added or the weakest conditions can be replaced with the better one.  
  
Based on above logic, here are the hints to troubleshoot the volume of trades for the given strategy based on its signal method (filtering system):  
\- if the strategy trades too often: increase or optimize its corresponding _SignalMethod_ param;  
\- if the strategy doesn't trade much or you want it to trade more often: decrease or reset _SignalMethod_ to 0, then optimize its value.

  * Edited 9:27pm  May 15, 2018 9:03pm | Edited 9:27pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11060713#post11060713 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I am first running it from 2014-2016 with everything enabled, then optimizing each type of signal (bands etc) and then combining everything to one set finally.
> 
> Ignored

Few hints on optimizations:  
\- I usually disable boosting (Boosting_Enabled=0) and actions (Account_Conditions_Active=0) when running optimizations, so you've pure technical results. Boosting and actions can be tested at the final test, whether they add some value on top of it or not.  
\- I also use CloseOrderAfterXHours=48, LotSize set to 0.01 and ProfitFactorMinToTrade/ProfitFactorMaxToTrade=0 specifically for the optimization tests (see [ea_default_sets()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-optimization-rules/blob/102493bd571deba7047f7223213ff98b10603017/Common/.init.rules.inc#L41)). So profits for orders opened after 2 days are not taken into the account, and lot size is not automatically increased with the balance, so you're relying on the very strict rules (all trades should be equal as possible, not dependent on the previous success or current balance).  
\- Above strict rules will not always give you the good results, only the right direction, but combining them with some later-stage params, they can hugely improve.  
\- Another benefit of setting fixed and minimum lot size (0.01), is that you want to open as many trades as possible (>1000), so you can optimize params based on the large dataset giving as much possible scenarios and different market conditions.  
\- I usually optimize each strategy on its own, then merge it with the others at the final tests when optimizing params which affects all strategies (see: [optimization tests for Strategies](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-optimization-rules/tree/102493bd571deba7047f7223213ff98b10603017/Strategies)).  
\- SignalMethod should be optimized only for the given strategy and its timeframe (in the isolated run, so every other strategy should be disabled), it's quicker and more reliable.  
\- If SignalMethod is too much filtered (less than <100 trades), that's sometimes bad, as you don't have enough dataset to optimize other params (in other words, the optimization results could be not reliable).  
\- Strategy-specific multi-timeframe-shared params such as Period_Ratio, SignalLevel, Applied_Price are tested after optimization of timeframe-specific param (such as SignalMethod).  
\- For very slow optimization tests, I use Control points to have some rough idea which value is better, but the results could not always be reliable.  
\- At the final tests, I test boosting on/off or/and actions on/off (or few specific actions), CloseOrderAfterXHours, RiskMargin, RiskRatio, RiskRatioDecreaseMethod/RiskRatioIncreaseMethod and similar.  
  

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11059783#post11059783 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> For CCI, is there a maximum value for the signal method? It just says "0-" with no maximum in the inputs. I looked through the source and couldn't find the information.
> 
> Ignored

Actually, the range for CCI is -63-63, similar for every other strategy (that is, not from 0, but from the negative corresponding value). So as [already explained](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11060574#post11060574) the 6 conditions, negative and positive numbers are basically the same conditions, but positives values trades with trend only, and negative values trades ignores the trend check. So 63 value means all 6 conditions need to match as well the trend need to match the type of order (buy for bullish trend, sell for bearish trend), where -63 will execute trades for all 6 conditions including trades against the trend. The trend logic is controlled by _TrendMethod_ param in v1.072 (based on bear/bull candles), and _TrendPeriod_ in v1.075 (based on RSI).  
For example, some strategies aren't really good at trading against the trend (such as Fractals, despite the conditions), so positive values should be set, some other strategies can work well when trading against the trend (like RSI). Including negative values, makes the optimization process twice as long.

> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Notes: 1. In backtest, EA blew the account in 3 months. 2. We can get a lot of rebates with this EA. 3. I'll post set file when I get home. 4. In live account tests, we might want to reduce the "minimum volume to open".
> 
> Ignored

v1.072 is risky, as it has some trouble closing good trades on time, and managing a lot of open trades at the same time can jump your equity up and down. Huge drops when having too many trades opened at the same time can kill the account. That's why further versions got better risk management logic (such as _RiskMarginPerOrder_ and _RiskMarginTotal_ params), but not optimized so well yet.

Usually slight changes in logic (like adding params which affect all strategies) requiring re-optimization of the whole EA. Didn't have time to do this for v1.75 as it's requiring a lot of effort. I'm improving the optimization system, so it can make the optimization process easier (I'll share it soon). Basically, what was in v1.72, it's also in v1.75, improved, but needs optimization.

> [Quoting kenorb](/thread/post/11076099#post11076099 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Also, I've got some question about the commission, whoever can answer. Commission: -$5640.98 Balance: $16319.80 Deposits: $5000.00 Does it mean EA suppose to earn $21319.8 in total, but out of which $5640.98 took broker? So it charged like over 25% of the earnings? High commission then. Wouldn't be more profitable to run with the spread broker? Or not? What do you think? {image}
> 
> Ignored

Hi ken,  
  
My broker offers 2 types of account:  
1\. No commission = 1.2 pip spread on EURUSD average  
2\. Commission = 0.2 pip spread on EURUSD average  
  
For 1 standard lot, I have a pip value of USD 10.0  
  
Since the EA traded 749.16 (crazy!!) standard lots this week, the total commission my broker took is about****:  
USD 1,498.00 due to spread (estimated)  
USD 5,640.98 due to commission  
USD 7,118.98 total  
  
In comparison, if I used the no commission account, my broker would get USD 8,989.92 (estimated)  
  
I used formula (spread x pip value (standard lot) x total lots traded)  
  
Cheers

I know of some good EAs with verified myfxbook performance:  
  
1\. MomentumEA - available in mql5 market, very expensive (USD 2,000), multicurrency, price action strategy, verified myfxbook  
  
2\. Filter Grid EA - has a free version, can work with single / multiple pairs, grid, verified myfxbook  
  
3\. You can also check Magix's thread (Lost Sock) here in FF, but please don't post backtest in his thread as it will definitely draw his ire.  
  
I'll try to look for some more.

  * [#227](/thread/post/11076857#post11076857 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 11:59pm  May 19, 2018 8:26pm | Edited 11:59pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting spojka](/thread/post/11076365#post11076365 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Only some problem with SL and TP, which are not the same on settings and on some open trades. Overall strategy looks very good and I am prepared to help with backtesting and forward testing if anybody needs help {image}
> 
> Ignored

Take profit/loss params could be confusing at the beginning, but most of the time these values are not taken into the account since each strategy has its own dynamic profit/loss param (it's overriding these defaults). So these params are only used when in strategy section you set _TrailingStopMethod/ProfitMethod_ to _Fixed_ or _Bi-way_ _:Fixed_. Basically, this acts like a neutral fixed starting-point which reads what-if profit/loss is 120/60, but at the end, the strategies find it least profitable so they override its value by its own thing. In general, each strategy has its own logic (controlled by params) when to set take-profit or stop-loss and they're not fixed, but dependent on the other technical indicators. For example, MA-based strategy can open the trade based on the value of _Moving Averages_ indicator, then take the profit when the price hits the upper line of Bands indicator, or hit the stop-loss based on another indicator like SAR or RSI (this is just the example, and this logic is fully configurable). There are over 55 combinations (each different method or indicator) how you can set your stop-loss or take-profit value dynamically, which makes 3025 (55*55) combinations in total how you can configure your stop-loss and take-profit per each strategy.

> [Quoting Degolep](/thread/post/11078915#post11078915 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} I've added your setfile but I get this error? {image}
> 
> Ignored

I believe you're using v1.075 (based on the Error 5006 which belong to the latest version). So if you're trying to load v1.072 SET file into v1.075 (based on the fact that posted SET file which you quoted was for v1.072) - it really won't work as the params are slightly different between the versions. In that case, you'll get the partial load breaking the whole logic. Secondly, when using v1.075 and you've got initialization issue, I've added a note to the [release](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/tag/v1.075) which params need to change (this was already mentioned few times).

  * Edited 7:32pm  May 21, 2018 7:20pm | Edited 7:32pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting cescof](/thread/post/11080563#post11080563 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Hy... i'm trying to use your set file.... but i'm quite sure i'have some problem on my platform because i've this expert error even if i have some orders placed.. Any suggests? Thanks Regards {image}
> 
> Ignored

These are just info messages, not the errors, they basically say the order suppose to be executed, but it didn't, as it would be too close to another one triggered from the same strategy (the safe distance is controlled by _MinPipGap_ value). Otherwise if _MinPipGap_ is set too low, you'll end up with too many similar orders. You can suppress these by disabling info messages. As far as I remember, I've lowered this kind of messages to debug type in the latest version.

  * [#252](/thread/post/11083101#post11083101 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:51am  May 22, 2018 6:25am | Edited 6:51am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

The problem with the older version v1.072 (such as _zeramlakireg_ account which got a lot of losses today) is how the boosting is applied, and not lowering lot sizes based on the risk and some flaws, which has been improved. One week was not enough to learn about market conditions and EA get too confident with its success rate by increasing lot sizes too much (I've described this in [post #85](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=10990723#post10990723) and [#155 about warm-up period](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11028805#post11028805)), that's why warm-up period has been introduced to test the market conditions for longer period of time with minimal lots. Most likely, the perfect market conditions last week, set too high boosting values for successful strategies which didn't work this week. The secondary problem, lack of optimization of take-profit values. So v1.072 showed some power, but it seems it's not so optimized, and needs some work (ideally done on the latest version). Last week was exciting, but this week showed some flaws and just demonstrated how much further work needs to be done in order to find some balance. Most of the params are customizable, so it's a matter of time and good optimization.  
  
Another issue now is that the auto lot size is re-calculated based on the current balance at every week (see: [StartNewWeek()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/blob/v1.072/src/EA31337.mq4#L4118)). Since the big loss happened today on Monday, now EA will use larger lot sizes to recover the funds, so it's got a challenge now.  
  
For people, who would like to run alternative forward testing, you may run v1.072 without boosting feature enabled.  
  
It's also worth to mention, that each run is very unique, it has its own stats, progress and learning ratio. The longer EA runs, the stats are more balanced. For example, _zeramlakireg_ account was run only for one week, progress was too good, then next week was very bad, which was not expected. Where _tazmaan_ account suffered a bit fewer losses, since it was running for the whole month, so the stats are more balanced.

The best is to identify which strategy is misconfigured via the order's magic number (see [post #174](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11041150#post11041150)), or stats, or by checking the generated report file. Then check the value of trailing stop for this strategy in the appropriate section, and re-optimize it.  
  

> [Quoting walesamuel](/thread/post/11083208#post11083208 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Is is possible to program this EA to wait 10 pips in profit before trailing and this first trail to give 3 pips profit and lock this?
> 
> Ignored

Since most of the trailing stops rely on indicator values, in some cases when calculated values are too close to the price, the fixed stop is set (as far as I remember). In other words, for some trailing methods, the price needs to move up in order the valid stop loss can be set.  
But I think I've slightly misunderstood your question, so I'll answer it again.  
  

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Is is possible to program this EA to wait 10 pips in profit before trailing and this first trail to give 3 pips profit and lock this? If this can be achieved that means it'll close in profit no matter what.

  
If you wait for 10 pips in profit before setting trailing stop, that means you won't have stop-loss set till then, so it's introducing the risk whereas EA has the policy to always set a stop-loss, no matter what. In most of the cases, setting stops (SL or TP) too close to the price will generate the losses due to broker's [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") or commission. The EA aims to not be a scalper, but generating larger profits, but it's possible to optimize it as a scalper.  
  
If this didn't answer your question, please elaborate.

> Thanks for your swift reply, would again look into this. I have an EA that sets its stop loss a bit wide to pave way for price flunctuation, it then waits for the price to move 9 or 10 pips and subsequently moves the stop loss from 200 points behind entry and place it 3 pips ahead of entry which secures 3 pips even if the price returns. This style wouldn't deplete your equity. Your EA is an advanced EA with user defined strategy. Please see if this style if possible for fine tuning or I would have to figure out what to do. I have disabled them on...
> 
> Ignored

Now I know what you mean by locking. The EA has two type of trailing types: one-way (locked) and bi-way.  
  
Example 1:  
T1_10_BARS_PEAK = 5, // 10 bars peak  
T2_10_BARS_PEAK = -5, // Bi-way: 10 bars peak  
The first method will move trailing stop by a distance of highest price from last 10 bars, but only one way (along with the price, securing the profit). Bi-way is opposite, will move two ways (without locking).  
  
Example 2:  
T1_MA_S = 19, // MA Slow  
T2_MA_S = -19, // Bi-way: MA Slow  
The first method will move trailing stop by the value of _Moving Average_ indicator and will use the locking (can move only one way along with the profit), the second will move both ways (exactly how _MA Slow_ indicator will move).  
  
Each trailing method got its corresponding locked version. See: [ENUM_TRAIL_TYPE enum](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/blob/v1.075/src/include/EA31337/ea-enums.mqh#L273). I'll add _Locked_ term to the opposite methods of _Bi-way_ , unless you can propose the better naming to differentiate these two.

The magic broke. It was very exciting last week, we beat all the competitions, unfortunately, I think the risk was set too high.  
  
You mentioned that you've increased _RiskMargin_ to 3.0, I think that's the main cause of the loss on your account.  
  
I've checked and v1.072 by default has _RiskMargin_ set to 1.0 (1%), and you've increased to risk by 3 times (3%)! So the risk was set way too high therefore the EA's lot sizes were calculated too large, and things went out of the control.  
  
Maybe you should re-run it with RiskMargin 1.0 or less![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

> [Quoting kenorb](/thread/post/11083366#post11083366 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Now I know what you mean by locking. The EA has two type of trailing types: one-way (locked) and bi-way. Example 1: T1_10_BARS_PEAK = 5, // 10 bars peak T2_10_BARS_PEAK = -5, // Bi-way: 10 bars peak The first method will move trailing stop by a distance of highest price from last 10 bars, but only one way (along with the price, securing the profit). Bi-way is opposite, will move two ways (without locking). Example 2: T1_MA_S = 19, // MA Slow T2_MA_S = -19, // Bi-way: MA Slow The first method will move trailing stop by the value of Moving...
> 
> Ignored

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

> [Quoting walesamuel](/thread/post/11085323#post11085323 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Many thanks for your help, I have done the trailing stop but this ea is losing 98% of the trades, please check the two log files (21st May & 22nd May attached. Maybe it'll give a clue as to where the problem lies. {file}
> 
> Ignored

You should use it only on EURUSD, as it hasn't been optimized for the other pairs. As far as I understand from your logs, you've tried to run it on over 10 different pairs. For different pairs, you'll have to use different SET file (alternative one were shared in this thread). Or generate and provide your own, so other can test. Currently, the EA works per single pair which was optimized to. And all existing versions and their default settings were optimized for EURUSD only. Maybe in future versions, we can make it work on multiple pairs, currently, it's designed to work only one specific one. Basically, the settings need to compatible with the market that you're running on.  
  

> [Quoting walesamuel](/thread/post/11085511#post11085511 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote}I am using version 1.75, do I need set files, and if so, where can I get them?
> 
> Ignored

No other set files apart from the default settings which have already embedded the best-known settings. You can optimize it on your own, or wait for the new set files, or next versions, to test the new improvements.  
  

> [Quoting walesamuel](/thread/post/11085323#post11085323 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Maybe it'll give a clue as to where the problem lies. {file}
> 
> Ignored

Thanks for the logs, I'll check them in details. However, there is not really any problem, the EA logic works as expected according to the configured params (which you haven't change I guess). I'm not advertising it as profitable (it all depends how much it's optimized for the given dataset, how you're using/running it, on what market, what broker, [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide")/commissions, leverage plus your trading knowledge, luck and hundred of other factors). In general, your outcome is tied to your time and effort you put into it (every run is unique and without understanding all the factors, you'll always fail). For sure it requires some work and optimization (as everything else), so please use it at your own risk. It's basically not perfect and it won't be. It's a powerful tool given for free (including the source code; it's one of its kind) with billions of billions of combinations and permutations fully controlled by the user according to his needs. The only missing part is to understand how it works and the ability to optimize it well (this is all that you need). You can also use it as the engine or framework, so you can configure your own unique way and/or develop new strategies which can be managed by the main algorithm.  
  
I'm aware that people expect something profitable and working out-of-box, and for free, with their minimal effort spent. That is not the case. The EA basically comes as it is, and it still requires a lot of work which can take further years (it's basically ongoing never-ending development process). In other words, there is nothing to blame, you just need good settings for the given pair and market conditions that you're running on and some awareness what's going on, so you can keep adjusting it to your needs. If you find the perfect configuration that works great for you, that's great, share it. But you need to put some effort into configuring it according to your needs. Therefore I won't be able to help with the losses when running on some random pairs unless you find some specific errors/bugs or logic flows within EA itself or propose the new improvements, so they can be considered.  
  
That's how Forex works. As one week you can win 250%, another lose (as we've seen). The challenge here is to find the balanced params. Nobody found the holy grail yet.

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting OzHopper](/thread/post/11093807#post11093807 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> For anyone interested in it's progress i've linked Trade Explorers to the currently running live trading account with EA31337 ver 1.072 under my profile. I'd link it here but unsure of the code to use like others have above. Also, is this error an issue?  
>  2018.05.24 18:08:49.474 EA31337-Lite-Full-v1.072 EURUSD,M1: **Info** (1132): OpenOrderIsAllowed: Maximum open and pending orders has reached the limit (MaxOrders).  
>  It's repeated down the list under every indicator but reads Maximum open and pending orders per...
> 
> Ignored

This is the information message, not the error, telling that you've reached maximum 'open and pending orders', based on the calculated limits for your balance. So the EA is driving on the full force. In other words, EA would like to open more orders, but it would be too risky given the calculated risk (such as balance). You can disable info messages if you wish, but it's not recommended.  
  

> [Quoting OzHopper](/thread/post/11093154#post11093154 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi everyone first post! I just wanted to say thankyou kenorb for all of your complex hard work that has gone into this project. I've had a little play and today dove straight in!! $1100 loaded into a live trading account with the files and version from this [post #9](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=10981913#post10981913) (v1.072) on MT4 latest release. It's been running 1 hourish so far current result is -$32 ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f605.png?v=15.1) OzHopper
> 
> Ignored

I wish you luck, however, if you're running v1.072 with the default settings, it's a bit unpredictable, as we've seen on the demo accounts. One week could go well, another not. Secondly, your performance also depends on the broker. If your [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") are too high, EA could generate the losses instead, so you should investigate first on the demo. It would be good if you can backtest it using your broker data for the latest few months and adjust for your needs.

> Ignored

Your calculated lot size 0.04 is higher than the minimal one due to your account leverage (the logic of [lot size is explained here](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/issues/50#issuecomment-391126755)). Since the market isn't in your favour, you get losses.  
  
Another thing, we can read from these lines:  
Initial deposit: 1000.00 EUR  
Total net profit: -149.25 EUR  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -5.57pips (+0.31/-5.88), Total orders: 6 (Won: 16.7% [1] / Loss: 83.3% [5]) - DeMarker M1  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -8.19pips (+0.31/-8.50), Total orders: 6 (Won: 16.7% [1] / Loss: 83.3% [5]) - DeMarker M5  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -5.77pips (+0.48/-6.25), Total orders: 5 (Won: 20.0% [1] / Loss: 80.0% [4]) - DeMarker M15  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -5.39pips (+0.31/-5.70), Total orders: 4 (Won: 25.0% [1] / Loss: 75.0% [3]) - DeMarker M30  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -1.63pips (+0.31/-1.94), Total orders: 2 (Won: 50.0% [1] / Loss: 50.0% [1]) - RSI M15  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -5.05pips (+0.31/-5.36), Total orders: 4 (Won: 25.0% [1] / Loss: 75.0% [3]) - RSI M30  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -2.20pips (+0.00/-2.20), Total orders: 2 (Won: 0.0% [0] / Loss: 100.0% [2]) - SAR M1  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -1.40pips (+0.00/-1.40), Total orders: 2 (Won: 0.0% [0] / Loss: 100.0% [2]) - SAR M5  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -1.83pips (+0.00/-1.83), Total orders: 1 (Won: 0.0% [0] / Loss: 100.0% [1]) - WPR M15  
Profit factor: 1.00, Total net profit: -6.31pips (+0.00/-6.31), Total orders: 4 (Won: 0.0% [0] / Loss: 100.0% [4]) - WPR M30  
  
That you didn't have enough trades to calculate the proper _profit factor_ (all are 1.0), you need at least 10-20 for each. So each strategy just barely traded, so EA doesn't know which one is successful. Secondly, it seems that you're like restarting EA every day, as you've send the report files for every day (whereas this file is generated only on restart/quit), with different amount of strategies enabled each time, so I think this is not going to work well. Currently, EA doesn't support loading the previous stats from the previous run, each time when you run, you start from scratch.  
  
If it's not you who restarting it, maybe your VPS keeps restarting?  
  
My suggestions: You need at least one week of the constant run, to know whether EA works for you or not, so the stats for strategies are populated properly and their profit factor (success rate), so it knows how to prioritize them. Since your account leverage is high (1:400), especially for such low balance, you'll see more losses in shorter amount of time if the market conditions are not in your favor, so you either need to lower your leverage (on your broker site or by contacting them), or set the lot size manually to 0.01 (instead of 0), so you can give more time for EA to adjust to the market conditions with lesser losses. If after a week, you still got the losses comparing to the other accounts, share the report files again, so we can see what we can read.  
  
\----  
  
Also, you've very low ticks per minute on your broker.  
Ticks per min (avg): 105  
Ticks per min (avg): 47  
Ticks per min (avg): 37  
Like something is wrong with your broker data. Not sure why. These values are usually over 200 on the demo/real run, especially on high-volume pairs such as EURUSD.

Everything is in the git repository. This was explained already in the first couple of posts, so please re-read as people had the same problems. If you carefully follow steps from [Compilation](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki/Compilation), and you clone the repo with \--recurse-submodules, you'll get all the folders populated, then checkout the v1.072 tag (git checkout v1.072). Then create symbolic links or copy these folders into appropriate places (MT4 include folder). If the steps aren't clear, create a new GitHub ticket. I won't be able to upload, as these files are constantly changing depending on the version you're trying to compile, so it'll be just more confusing and I'm sure you'll get into further problems, so the only way of managing these files is using Git. Secondly, the full sources were already uploaded into this thread, including these folders, so just check the attachment list of this thread. In case you've got these folders right, and you're missing only a few files, then you need to make sure you're using the right version of the class repo.

  * [#314](/thread/post/11108019#post11108019 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:22am  May 29, 2018 5:54am | Edited 6:22am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting Tabary](/thread/post/11107888#post11107888 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} is it the one like this sir? {file}
> 
> Ignored

That's the one, but it's between 2018.04.12-2018.05.24, not 2018.03.01-2018.05.31, still fine. I can't see any issues at the first glance.  
Few notes, you've got 66 ticks per minute in average, so it's like one tick per second which is low comparing to the data which I've used for optimization, but probably it shouldn't matter, not sure.  
Another thing, your account has quite low leverage (1:50), especially for such small deposit, so $2468.14 is required to open one lot (which is a bit high), therefore after calculation your account could only open 2 orders per strategy (25 in total), which is not a lot and could affect the results. Basically, EA was optimized with the minimum of $2000 deposit with at least 1:100 or 1:200 leverage. So having low leverage for such small deposit could make the negative results especially for such leverage, as EA didn't have enough flexibility and opportunities to open the successful trades (by trial and error). My suggestion is to try to backtest it again with the higher leverage (like 1:100 or 1:200) and see if you'll get the different results.  
For the next versions, I'll have to test the accounts with different account leverages and see how can affects the results. I'll compare your results with my configuration this week and let you know.

Some stats from different brokers and account types:  
  
FXOpen STP: 38 ticks per min  
[IronFX](/brokers/ironfx "View IronFX Broker Profile") standard: 87 ticks per min  
IronFX Abs zero: 516 ticks per min  
IronFX STP/ECN: 478 ticks per min  
  
I don't think there is a general correlation ticks per min with performance (IronFX STP/ECN has 43% max dd) but maybe it does factor in some how. Best performance so far is IronFX abs zero (10% max dd).

  * [#322](/thread/post/11110511#post11110511 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:37pm  May 29, 2018 8:27pm | Edited 8:37pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11109149#post11109149 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Some stats from different brokers and account types: FXOpen STP: 38 ticks per min IronFX standard: 87 ticks per min IronFX Abs zero: 516 ticks per min IronFX STP/ECN: 478 ticks per min I don't think there is a general correlation ticks per min with performance (IronFX STP/ECN has 43% max dd) but maybe it does factor in some how. Best performance so far is IronFX abs zero (10% max dd).
> 
> Ignored

With Dukascopy dataset, I had 570 ticks per minute for backtesting. Lesser tick data theoretically shouldn't make the difference, but it could be actually opposite.  
There is a _TickIgnoreMethod_ param (logic in ShouldIgnoreTick()) when it is set to a positive value (range: 0-5), it ignores certain ticks. The results should be similar, but they're not.  
  
For example (full test results in the attachment):  
Profit Total trades Profit factor Expected Payoff Drawdown $ Drawdown %  
10616.63 959 1.25 11.07 6384.50 43.76 TickIgnoreMethod=0  
7434.37 805 1.29 9.24 5797.92 42.78 TickIgnoreMethod=1  
2688.45 584 1.12 4.60 6466.84 49.67 TickIgnoreMethod=2  
2620.59 558 1.12 4.70 5892.46 42.23 TickIgnoreMethod=3  
  
Where 0 value means all ticks, 1 - ticks on open bar, 2 - open, low and high ticks only (OHLC), 3 - one tick per bar. So higher number of ticks can produce 5 times better results for backtesting. Why is that, I'm not sure. Possibly EA can catch more opportunities/trades earlier when there are more ticks (as indicator values can be wilder), but this needs some analysis. So for further versions, it would be better to get away from relying on ticks data, but standardize the input by going towards candle analysis (HST), so the input data is more consistent and easier to optimize. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: txt](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/txt.gif) [All-Trade-TickIgnoreMethod--EURUSD-10000USD-2016year-20spread-DS-test.txt](/attachment/file/2826615?d=1527592861) 1 KB | 192 downloads

> [Quoting Tabary](/thread/post/11108813#post11108813 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote}about the date time on the testing i set it to 2018.03.01-2018.05.31, but after the test, the file i get is 2018.04.12-2018.05.24....... which confuse me a bit right now...... is it possible that the broker did not allowed for a longer testing time???? {image} {file}
> 
> Ignored

That means you're lack of proper data for these dates. Testing on the broker data isn't reliable, as there could be too many gaps and low-quality data. You set testing from 01.03, but your data starts from 12.04, you want to end on 31.05, but your tick data stops on 24.05, so you can't rely on this.  
  

> [Quoting itsshark](/thread/post/11108976#post11108976 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi there, i'm new to forex, just started like 3 months ago, i'm testing your EA version 1.072 today with the optimization given from this thread (EURUSD), looking good so far . I've been trying out the latest version, 1.075 but it wont trade, for hours the indicator appear but haven't been able to trade, do you know why? and my question is, is it safe to just use the version 1.072? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

1.075 got fewer strategies enabled due to some optimization issues, so it trades less often compared to 1.072. You can always try re-enabling strategies which were enabled for 1.072 and see if that helps.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Man , my mind says go live with it , BUT what if !! hehehe btw if i want to reduce the lot size where to change ? i am using the default settings but i want to make the lot size less is lot auto =1% is the lowest ?
> 
> Ignored

You can lower _RiskMargin_ param to _0.5_ (0.5% per trade), alternatively _RiskRatio_ to _0.5_. Also, try to lower _BoostTrendFactor_ param to _1.1_ or _1.2_. Another way, to keep the lots to the minimum, is to disable _Boosting_ section. These changes should generate smaller lot sizes.

  * [#347](/thread/post/11112890#post11112890 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:18am  May 30, 2018 7:43am | Edited 8:18am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting Singh1](/thread/post/11112834#post11112834 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} I see everyone is posting nice results but when I do back test it blows up in the dirt. I can't figure out what am I doing wrong.{image} {image}
> 
> Ignored

In my opinion, all 90/99% backtesting (where data is converted using old unsupported scripts) provides just fake and unreliable results (used commonly by people who're not aware of wrongdoing or by the scammers) and I believe most of the EAs are backtested in the wrong way, but the majority believes it's the right way, that's why all of them struggling to be profitable despite showing the perfect curves. In one screenshot you've got 22 mismatched charts errors, these are the data errors (this should not happen), and since you've set the files to read-only (I assume), the platform doesn't have the ability to correct the errors. What you see in nice green bar - 90%, it is the fake value hardcoded by the script in FXT file (that's why you was asked to set the file as read-only, I believe). If you drop the read-only flag, most likely the files would be wiped out by the platform and marked as the corrupted and platform simply won't run the test. Same for the screenshot with _n/a_ (platform is confused by the invalid value which you're trying to force). These all forward-results just showing it's most likely the truth. For more explanation, check [post #22](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=10982286#post10982286). Basically, I'm using completely different scripts for optimization and backtesting on which I'm relying on (which now I'm convinced even more, that my method is more reliable than the common FXT-read-only aka "99%" modelling method). Check the steps described on '[Backtesting in MT4](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki/Backtesting-in-MT4)' page which I've written which uses the more reliable method (which uses ready-made FXT/HST files or use the Python scripts). I'll soon share the easier method for backtesting. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [4 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Edited 9:17am  May 30, 2018 9:03am | Edited 9:17am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting Singh1](/thread/post/11112944#post11112944 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> One question, should I set TP to auto or there is a recommended TP and SL?
> 
> Ignored

The EA is using different approach for TP/SL comparing to other EAs which is by using dynamic indicator values per strategy-basis (e.g., see: [post #258](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11083366#post11083366)), so there is no auto, or single TP/SL param to change, but multiple places. TP/SL are set in form of trailing stops per strategy. The default settings are the recommended one unless you can optimize the better one. To change TP/SL, you need to find the strategy of your choice in the list of params (grouped by sections), then adjust it. If you need to set the fixed one, there is _Fixed_ value as well (but it's not recommended). So there are no auto values for TP/SL, just default settings based on the optimization results.

I've already shared the set file for EURUSD only TE. Just look it up in the attahments (paperclip icon on top of the page).  
  
The mql market has a lot of EAs doing 1,000% daily in backtests but will blow your account in a couple of days (even hours)!  
  
So, don't trust your backtest/optimization if you are not kenorb. XD  
  
Just forward test the EA.  
  
Also, don't expect other account's performance to be replicated in yours. You will start forward test in a different market condition and your account history (where the EA bases its lot sizing) are different.  
  
Cheers!

Personally, I forward test an EA to be familiar with how it trades. Especially how it opens the lot size in relation to my account size. We have different brokers, leverages, capital, risk tolerance, etc.  
  
IMO, if you have not forward tested an EA in demo using your prefered broker, leverage, and capital which you plan to use live, don't even go live with any EA.  
  
Edit:  
Regarding backtesting ver 1.072, I was not able to find any range of date where the EA was profitable in my backtests. It always blew up the account. I used 90% data quality with no mismatches. Yet, the result of the TE is drastically different.

  * [#360](/thread/post/11114944#post11114944 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited May 31, 2018 1:56am  May 30, 2018 9:13pm | Edited May 31, 2018 1:56am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

I think people are too much focusing on the old version, keep running the same default configuration over and over again without changing anything, then they see the first week to be very profitable (then other people are panicking to follow the same), then the next week goes wrong and everybody is blaming EA. Unfortunately, the v1.072 with its default settings isn't balanced out, and it's not suitable for live and it was already mentioned (at least not with the default params). If you'd like to avoid high lot sizes, try at least turning off the boosting, then try again.  
There were several fixes improved in the further versions, it may not give you 100% a week, but it aims to be more balanced.  
  
For example, can anybody test the next version, which is the v1.073? It trades over 10 times less often than v1.072, but the logic should be very similar. Also, v1.073 was optimized and tested on the larger dataset (2014-2016, instead of 2014-2015). I'm attaching the backtesting results to compare v1.072 vs v1.073.  
  
\----  
  
EA31337-Lite-Backtest-v1.072  
Symbol EURUSD (Euro vs US Dollar)  
Period 30 Minutes (M30) 2014.01.06 00:00 - 2015.12.30 23:30 (2014.01.01 - 2015.12.31)  
Bars in test 24856 Ticks modelled 154351318 Modelling quality 89.64%  
Initial deposit 10000.00 Spread 20  
Total net profit 18930.69 Gross profit 91018.87 Gross loss -72088.18  
Profit factor 1.26 Expected payoff 3.25  
Absolute drawdown 1619.57 Maximal drawdown 9401.33 (30.06%) Relative drawdown 30.06% (9401.33)  
Total trades 5829 Short positions (won %) 4460 (48.68%) Long positions (won %) 1369 (42.00%)  
Profit trades (% of total) 2746 (47.11%) Loss trades (% of total) 3083 (52.89%)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: EURUSD-10000USD-2014-2016year-10spread-M30-DS-test.gif
Size: 19 KB](/attachment/image/2828915/thumbnail?d=1527683698)](/attachment/image/2828915?d=1527683698)   

  
  
\----  
  
Few notes:  
\- v1.072 got max 9401USD (30% DD) in the drawdown in 2 years, and v1.073 got only 4601USD in DD in 3 years, which is two times less (so safer to use).  
\- v1.073 trades 13 times less per year (642/3y=214 vs 5829/2y=2914.5), so that means you don't waste your money into broker's fees/[spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") or/and commissions.  
\- [Expected payoff](https://www.mql5.com/en/articles/1486) is 2 times higher for v1.073 (6.71 vs 3.25).  
\- Please note that above 2 charts are for spread 20, which is very high (most of EAs are tested with 10 or less). If you've got lesser spreads with your brokers, profits can potentially double, as you pay less to the broker.

The v1.075 is trading even lesser, as it only few strategies enabled as it was aiming for the tests with even higher [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") (like 40, but then optimization system disabled half of the strategies), and people start complaining it doesn't trade for hours, secondly, it got a small startup init issue so people are a bit confused how to use it, so probably it needs more work. On the other hand, since few first posts, people got excited about 1.072, so moving to 1.073 is the less drastic change for now, so we can compare the results, understand the weaknesses and move forward. I don't know the versions beyond that (can't find the full backtest for 1.074), I'll have to dig the tests or re-run, but further versions weren't optimized after the logic changes/improvements, so they may not work well as good as the previous one with the defaults. I'll provide soon the backtests for all the versions so they can be compared.

Furthermore, it seems v1.074 got some issues, as only 3 type of indicators are enabled by default, and out of 5 strategies (Envelopes M15&M30, MACD M30, RSI M15&M30), for some reason only one (MA M15) was profitable. The results are still good, but something went wrong during the process. So I'm attaching backtest for v1.074 for 2015 which I've found, as can't find any for the other years. Of course, you can re-enable the other ones manually using params which you like and test.  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: EURUSD-2000USD-2015year-20spread-M30-DS-test.gif
Size: 17 KB](/attachment/image/2829087/thumbnail?d=1527689177)](/attachment/image/2829087?d=1527689177)   

  
  
EA31337-Lite-Backtest-v1.074  
Period 30 Minutes (M30) 2015.01.06 00:00 - 2015.12.30 23:30 (2015.01.01 - 2015.12.31)  
Bars in test 12404 Ticks modelled 80271172 Modelling quality 89.28%  
Initial deposit 2000.00 Spread 20  
Total net profit 1089.81 Gross profit 3992.04 Gross loss -2902.22  
Profit factor 1.38 Expected payoff 4.10  
Absolute drawdown 565.96 Maximal drawdown 782.01 (35.29%) Relative drawdown 35.29% (782.01)  
Total trades 266 Short positions (won %) 87 (29.89%) Long positions (won %) 179 (33.52%)  
Profit trades (% of total) 86 (32.33%) Loss trades (% of total) 180 (67.67%)  
  
Still isn't bad as for only one strategy (other 4 not profitable), so I'm not sure exactly what went wrong. It probably requires optimization of all the disabled strategies and re-enabling them. Please also note that the above test is for a low deposit of 2k USD, not 10k as previous ones (so it got less flexibility), and high spread of 20 points.  
  
Then v1.075 got only logic improvements and fixes, no optimization has been done, probably that's why it doesn't trade often (as per above). So it's on the current todo list.

> 
> {quote}Also the backtests you ran were those on Mt4?
> 
> Ignored

Yes, these tests were run using MT4 platform run under Linux Ubuntu using automated scripts. Exact details of the dataset which was used to run the tests are also embedded onto image (period, how many ticks/bars and the result it-self).

  * [#373](/thread/post/11117483#post11117483 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:07am  May 31, 2018 6:00am | Edited 8:07am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting oocat0227](/thread/post/11116745#post11116745 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi all seems different broker have different trades I test old version. 1.072, use default setting (on EURUSD M15) at the same time. this week. a) on SVSFX demo account, when I enable the EA, it open the trade Sell and Buy on my MT4 b) on IronFX demo account , when I enable the EA, it only open the SELL c) on FXTM-cent demo account , it only open Sell trade. does someone have the same problem? I will try other version...
> 
> Ignored

Some strategies are set to trade with trend, some aren't. Check the [trend detection description in post #178](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11051153#post11051153) and [#180](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11051636#post11051636). So possibly different strategies are triggered on different brokers, but you'll have to compare the [magic numbers](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11041150#post11041150), which are probably different. There are hundreds of factors taken into the account (like conditions and filtering systems in place) which are affecting how EA opens the trades, like slight price differences between brokers can trigger different conditions, also account balance/stats, broker spreads/leverage, existing orders, calculated lot size, free margins, slight delays, and many other factors could trigger different trades. You can also take the screenshots of the screen and compare the differences, or compare the initialization and trade logs which can give you more information. Another way is to enable debug messages.  
Basically, each run is unique and difficult to predict why certain trades are triggered, and other not on different brokers. This will require a new feature focusing on it and logging that kind of things. Normally without any filters, EA could potentially receive hundreds of buy/sell signals per minute, and logging such data, such as why certain orders weren't triggered, it can only slow the EA and generate very huge logs.

  * Edited 8:41pm  May 31, 2018 8:13pm | Edited 8:41pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

[quote=chrisdk2017;11118744]

> [Quoting kenorb](/thread/post/11116487#post11116487 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Could you show us the Docker way? I guess this is for the latest version, 1.075?
> 
> Ignored

I've published [Docker container](https://github.com/EA31337/FX-MT-VM/blob/master/Dockerfile) for backtesting and supported containers can be pulled from [Docker's hub](https://hub.docker.com/r/ea31337/fx-mt-vm/). The main container (latest) doesn't have any backtest data by default, so it needs to download each time, but in the next days/weeks I can provide tagged containers per each pair and year, so they'll come with data ready for testing, so all files needs to be downloaded only once (so once you've got container downloaded, backtest or optimization test can be started in few seconds with a single command). Here is the [list of supported historical data](https://github.com/FX-Data) (I'm still populating the data, DS means _Dukascopy_ feed). These repositories consist of raw CSV files which are converted to MT4 HST/FXT format by the scripts for all the timeframes (including custom ones). On request, any source/broker data can be added, including cryptocurrencies, so the new data can be used for backtesting/optimization.  
  
Once [Docker](https://docs.docker.com/docker-for-windows/) is installed (on Windows, Linux or macOS), you can pull the container by (run in the terminal/cmd):  
docker pull ea31337/fx-mt-vm  
  
Then for help run: docker run ea31337/fx-mt-vm help  
For backtesting param, run: docker run ea31337/fx-mt-vm run_backtest  
  
To run the backtest, you can use supported params as displayed by above help command.  
  
Here is the example command for backtesting v1.075 for 2017.01-02 on EURUSD with spread 10:  
docker run -e BOOT_CODE='file_get [https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/r...ull-v1.075.ex4](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/download/v1.075/EA31337-Lite-Full-v1.075.ex4)' ea31337/fx-mt-vm run_backtest -e EA31337 -y 2017 -m 1-2 -p EURUSD -s 10 -v  
  
To test the different version, change it in two places in above command.  
  
There are many custom params, so backtest or optimization tests can be fully customized. In the next weeks, I'll be improving and simplifying backtesting processes for Docker, so any version of EA can be re-optimized. So if you need any particular feature, please let me know. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [1 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> [Quoting SlicEnDicE](/thread/post/11119589#post11119589 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> What it lacks, is some "brains" that would allow the EA to dynamically adjust based on market conditions.
> 
> Ignored

I was thinking exactly the same way. I was attempting to add RSI_DynamicPeriod param (some logic in RSI_CheckPeriod()), but I don't know any equation which allows detecting the current best period (without trials and errors), and the optimization process only finds the average one, so it's something to work on (it's the limitation of all EAs based on technical indicators). The larger optimization period, the values are actually more flatten, so it's safer to use, but less flexible and profitable at the same time.  
  
I'll be working on the refactor soon, I hope, so I was planning to add dummy trades, which aims to be the simulation of the real trades, but only happening in the EA's memory, so based on the dummy/hidden profit happening in the memory (like opening dummy trades for different periods and comparing the profits), EA can find the best params (such as current best periods and other params), for the current dataset, in order to use it before actually starting to trade, then opening only certain type of trades after they were tested and proven in the memory.  
  
Another method is to tap the params into machine learning algorithm and calculate the best params along as the EA trades.

  * [#383](/thread/post/11119771#post11119771 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 11:44pm  May 31, 2018 8:55pm | Edited 11:44pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11119676#post11119676 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Is it possible to make a Docker container including EURUSD data 2007-current? I don't think it makes sense to use earlier data but some people go back to 2003. Maybe there is a file size limitation of the containers.
> 
> Ignored

You can use -y option for any year which is listed in [FX-Data-EURUSD-DS repo](https://github.com/FX-Data/FX-Data-EURUSD-DS) (check the _Branch_ select list, or [tag release files](https://github.com/FX-Data/FX-Data-EURUSD-DS/releases)), and it'll be downloaded automatically from this repo. There is data available between 2007 and 2017. Usually I upload the current year once it's finished, but I can also upload 2018 partially before that. There are also few combinations of multiple years such as 2011-2015, 2015-2017. I'll publish containers including the data inside soon, so downloading the container will have everything included. Using -m is optional, you can use -m1-2 for the first 2 months, and when you don't specify -m, the whole year is tested.  
  
The actual result files can be generated and published on your host machine, or uploaded anywhere. I'm working on it to test and improve this process as well.  
  
Using containers, you can run backtests/optimization tests non-interactively and in parallel on the cloud (any cloud that can support Docker containers, and most of them do). So it's very powerful tool. Something like MT5 got the optimization on the cloud, but this method gives you more flexibility. Potentially it can support MT5 backtesting as well.  
  

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11119676#post11119676 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Is it possible to make a Docker container including EURUSD data 2007-current? Maybe there is a file size limitation of the containers.
> 
> Ignored

To answer your question from the different point. To test the full period since 2007, it requires a lot of memory, processing and time. Initially, I was using Vagrant (similar to Docker) to automate the tests. Testing 2 years in a row was challenging as it was very slow and memory hungry given the number of ticks (~150mln ticks), then I've advanced to 3 years (~350mln ticks), which also takes very long time and MT4 is using a lot of memory. I've already created dataset for 2011-2015 (4 years), but I think there was a problem running it, but I'll need to check again. The first limitation probably is with the platform, as far as I remember, the FXT files cannot be bigger than few GB (2 or 4). If you pass that limitation, it still can go out-of-memory, so most likely MT4 platform won't run the test. So for easier testing and to avoid headaches, I prefer to backtest each year separately, also to not rely on the success and higher balance from the previous periods, and to test the different start. But I can also provide backtesting for the 4-10 years in a row, if that will work.

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11126695#post11126695 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote}{quote} How do you start an optimization? Maybe this is not available yet? I guess one should enable only part of the profitable strategies first and then optimize each one like you already explained.
> 
> Ignored

It's supported, all the optimization was done using the scripts. You need to pass -o param to run_backtest script to activate the optimization mode. Here is the example syntax:  
run_backtest.sh -x -o -t -v -I TestModel=0 -S ValidateSettings=0,WriteReport=0 -E maxdrawdown_enable=1,maxdrawdown=50 -f $SET_PATH/EA31337.set -e EA31337 -c USD -p EURUSD -d 10000 -s 10 -y 2017 -m 1-12 -D 5 -P M30 -b DS -M 4.0.0.1010 -i $RULES_PATH/Common/.init.rules.inc -i $RULES_PATH/$RULEFILE.rule -r ReportName -O /opt/results  
  
Most of the params are optional, or you can adjust to your needs. Most important is to pass set file with -f. Either you can prepare SET file ready for optimization, or you can use [rules files](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-optimization-rules) which will parse the SET and prepare the file according to which param you want to optimize for MT4 optimization process (e.g. to optimize MA profit-take load the Strategy-MA-All-MA_TrailingProfitMethod.rule file). Then the results are generated in the specified output dir. With Docker, you can mount your external dir by -v (e.g. -v /LOCAL/PATH:/opt/results:rw) so your results are generated on your local folder. I haven't tested it with Docker yet, but it should just work, and I'll be improving the process further to simplify it.  
  

> [Quoting chrisdk2017](/thread/post/11126695#post11126695 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote}{quote} I guess one should enable only part of the profitable strategies first and then optimize each one like you already explained.
> 
> Ignored

When you'll use the provided rule files, they're automatically designed to disable all the other strategies (by modifying the SET file) and optimize only one specific strategy at a time with the fixed lot size and other strict rules, to only focus on the specific param.

  * Edited 11:56pm  Jun 3, 2018 11:14pm | Edited 11:56pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting Iry](/thread/post/11128185#post11128185 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> What is the range for the signal level? {image} Thanks all![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f600.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

Awesome results you've got, especially for such a high spread.  
  
The signal level range depends on the technical indicator which strategy is using, so there are no fixed ranges, and it'll be difficult to standarize all of them into fixed range. It's basically the shift from the value which is produced by the given technical indicator. The easiest would be to check the code logic in corresponding Trade_... function.  
  
It's not clear which strategy you're talking, but let's give as the example the RSI, and the following logic:  
case ORDER_TYPE_BUY: result = rsi[period][CURR] < (50 - signal_level);  
case ORDER_TYPE_SELL: result = rsi[period][CURR] > (50 + signal_level);  
So the reasonable signal level is starting from 20 (so you will get 30 for buy, and 70 value for sell), then increasing it to 40 makes 10 vs. 90, which is already extreme, so making it 50 and beyond, you won't get any trades, as RSI technical indicator operates between 0 and 100. And setting it too low, like between 1-20 most likely will produce too many trades. That kind of range is similar to CCI and WPR.  
  
For other strategies where base indicators are like MA or Alligator, where the indicator values corresponding to the pair prices, the signal level is basically the distance in pips. So 0 means the original exact signal condition, 0.5 means half a pip, 1.0 means a pip away from the original value. Negative values mean the opposite (like triggering the signals right before the MA cross happens).  
  
So basically, for MA strategy/indicator, it's the distance between MA Fast and Medium on cross condition, so positive values will trigger signal after the cross happened, and negative values mean the opposite, will trigger the signal right before the MA cross happens.  
  
For Alligator, it's similar, so it's the distance between Lips/Teeth lines, and Teeth/Jaw lines. For MACD, it's the the distance between main and signal line in pips (signal level set to zero, means no extra distance, therefore the original, usual condition). E.g.  
double gap = signal_level * pip_size;  
case ORDER_TYPE_BUY: result = macd[period][CURR][MODE_MAIN] > macd[period][CURR][MODE_SIGNAL] + gap; // MACD rises above the signal line.  
case ORDER_TYPE_SELL: result = macd[period][CURR][MODE_MAIN] < macd[period][CURR][MODE_SIGNAL] - gap; // MACD falls below the signal line.  
  
For some strategies like Bands, Envelopes, the signal level is not implemented yet. And for some, like Fractals, the param is not compatible, due to lack of dynamic values, so some other similar value needs to be used.  
  
So in general, some signal levels should be increased with smaller steps like (0.1-0.2), some with integers (1-2), so while optimizing, you should know by trial and error how much it changes the results.  
  

> [Quoting Iry](/thread/post/11128185#post11128185 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 1\. Why the maximal drawdown value is different in the backtest report and journal details? The backtest report show maximal drawndown is $111.62 But the journal is written as $32.5? Which 1 is correct?
> 
> Ignored

One of these drawdowns isn't correct, so it's most likely the bug of the calculation function (as it's calculated independently from MT4) or due to some other factors. The logic is in [CalculateSummary()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/ce7f55146a29d6015ac3fce319162cd64e387ab1/SummaryReport.mqh#L171) (SummaryReport class).

Many thanks for the quick and helpful response! I followed your advice and all errors but the copy struct disappeared:  
  
'=' - structure have objects and cannot be copied Trade.mqh 60 18  
  
To solve this last issue, I changed the code in Trade.mqh to copy the structure parameters one by one. Here is my solution it just in case somebody has got the same issue:  
  
void Trade(TradeParams &_params) {  
// trade_params = _params; -> this didn't work on my MQ4 version, so copying the parameters one by one  
trade_params.account = _params.account;  
trade_params.chart = _params.chart;  
trade_params.slippage = _params.slippage;  
  
trade_params.account = (CheckPointer(trade_params.account) == POINTER_INVALID ? new Account : trade_params.account);  
trade_params.chart = (CheckPointer(trade_params.chart) == POINTER_INVALID ? new Chart : trade_params.chart);  
}  
  
Now the EA successfully compiles.

> Disliked

> {quote} Lately I was doing some research on the subject as a prep for converting my own EAs to MT5. The most challenging part is the trade management. Luckily for late comers like me, others have done some of the work already and there is a library out there to help with the conversion: <https://www.ea-coder.com/convert-mql4-to-mql5/>
> 
> Ignored

EA got its own libraries/classes/methods implemented which work for both MT4 and MT5 at the same time (using preprocessor conditional compilation directives), so no need for extra conversions or external libraries. Support for MT5 code is already in the advanced stage, so in this case, the general articles won't help much. These are only for some simple conversion.  
  
The current challenge is to implement asynchronous trades (MT5) along with the synchronous trades (MT4). Most of the forum posts say it's not possible, but EA aims at implementing something despite what other people claim, but it takes time.

You don't need coding, EA got parameterized condition-action system, so you can setup action to close trades on the direction change. But I don't think many people tried that. Many people suggest something without realizing it's already there.  
So basically using actions, you can setup closure of the trades (such as all, only the one with the trend, or against the trend, or losing once, or profitable, or whatever group you choose), on the indicator change value such as Moving Average Fast is going opposite direction to Slow one, or any other market event condition (on a buy or sell signal of any supported indicator such as RSI, or 28+ of other).  
Please test and let me know if this is what you're looking for.

  * [#405](/thread/post/11176722#post11176722 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 9:24pm  Jun 18, 2018 9:05pm | Edited 9:24pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting Loqito](/thread/post/11176101#post11176101 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I could not find how to change the main trend detection setting. It should be more sensitive. Under the main trend I mean the one that is shown on the chart. I have noticed that it continues to show previous trend direction and EA opens new countertrend orders even hours after the trend has changed. And this causes terrible losses.
> 
> Ignored

For changing trend detection sensitivity, you need to optimize _TrendMethod_ param for v1.072, or _TrendPeriod_ in v1.075 (based on RSI). Related posts [#178](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11051153#post11051153)-[#180](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11051636#post11051636), [#189](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11053558#post11053558), [#197](https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=11060850#post11060850) (2nd part).  
In v1.072, when optimizing _TrendMethod_ param, you're basically changing the sensitivity on the timeframe basis, so you're basically telling EA which timeframe should get the higher priority to tell about the main trend (check GetTrend() in Trend class for logic).  
In v1.075, the trend is based on the RSI and uses params such as: _TrendPeriod (the main param)_ , _RSI_Period_ and _RSI_Applied_Price_ (uses some values from RSI strategy) to calculate the trend strength between -0.5 and 0.5 where range between -0.1 and 0.1 is considered the neutral trend (no trades), and value below or above 0.3 is considered as the strong trend, so you're in full control how sensitive is the trend detection.
