  * [#411](/thread/post/12105972#post12105972 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:23am  Mar 13, 2019 12:44am | Edited 2:23am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

The version v1.072 was optimized very long time ago, and market conditions changes every year, and further versions I've confirmed them broken.  
  
However, finally I've manage to release the new version v1.076 which you can find at <https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases>  
  
Also attached here: 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: ex4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/ex4.gif) [EA31337-Lite-v1.076.ex4](/attachment/file/3263426?d=1552404575) 981 KB | 349 downloads 

.  
  
I didn't have time to test it on demo, my main focus was to produce good optimization results for 2018, so I've no idea how it performs on demo accounts. What I know, it generates a lot of trades, so **please use it with caution**.  
  
Note: **Use this version only against EURUSD pair with accounts with spread lower than 10** , as this is what it was optimized for. If you've account with higher [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide"), try on the demo first, but it's better to wait for further releases which can improve support for higher spreads, otherwise you can try to disable some lower-timeframe strategies. It was also tested with deposit of 10k USD, if you've lower deposit, please also test it on demo first for couple of weeks if it can adjust to your market conditions and current account balance.  
  
Suggested run:  
\- Timeframe M30 or M15, but it really shouldn't make any difference.  
\- EURUSD with spread 10 or lower.  
\- Default settings.  
  
Here are the results for EURUSD 2018 with spread 10:  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 54167029-d1907d00-445f-11e9-9801-2aad0072d7ad.png
Size: 42 KB](/attachment/image/3263452/thumbnail?d=1552404968)](/attachment/image/3263452?d=1552404968)   

  
  
Note: The reason why it's not curved to the end is, because it was only optimized for the first 6 months due to huge amount of computation involved while optimizing parameters, so dealing with the unknown data on the 2nd half of the year which was never optimized for is actually pretty well in my opinion.  
  
I've created EA Tester scripts which you can easily backtest EA with a single command.  
  
After installing [Docker](https://www.docker.com/get-started) (should work for Windows, macOS and Linux), you can run the following command in your operating system command-line terminal:  
  

Inserted Code
    
    
    docker run ea31337/ea-tester:EURUSD-2018-DS run_backtest -v -e https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/download/v1.076/EA31337-Lite-v1.076.ex4

  
Here is the recorded terminal demo how the backtesting using Docker is performed: <https://asciinema.org/a/233268> (press play button after clicking).  
  
I haven't tested it for 2019, so please let me know. For any bugs you find, please report them at [GitHub](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/issues). We've also group at Telegram IM at <https://t.me/EA31337> if you need any quicker response, as I'm not very active on this forum. I'm usually replying the private messages here after couple of months later as the interface is not very intuitive, sorry![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) Also, to let you know, I don't look for any work or projects to work on (other indicators or EAs), as I've received couple of messages like that.  
  
If you'd like to compile the project or read more about it, please check the following [wiki pages](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki).  
  
I'm planning to release further improved versions soon which can definitely beat the above results.

I think it's a MT4 platform bug, as it works when backtesting, the problem is when attaching to the chart. Somebody should report it as a bug to MT4 support (they've removed my accounts for no reason, so I can't). It was compiled using MetaEditor 5.0.0.1966.  
  
Anyway, I've recompiled it again, and this version should work: [https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/r...ite-v1.076.ex4](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/download/v1.076/EA31337-Lite-v1.076.ex4)

Make sure the spread is 10 or below, the test is done for every tick, for at least few months, it also depends on the broker data, so the broker backtest could be not reliable if the data doesn't have enough ticks (there need to be at least few ticks per each minute). Otherwise, I don't know, there could be some other variables come into play (leverage, high spread/commissions, starting deposit, lack of tick data, etc).

  * [#428](/thread/post/12289286#post12289286 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:30am  May 24, 2019 1:31am | Edited 2:30am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting mankindeg](/thread/post/12289234#post12289234 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Okay, so the setfile is actually just the default settings then? Also I notice in the journal that some indicators are missing. For example, something like: Error (5148): InitStrategy: Cannot initialize indicator for the Alligator M30 strategy!
> 
> Ignored

That means M30 timeframe historical data could be not available at the time of the run. As far as I know, MT4 platform got the bug, that if you run on M1, it may not load M30 correctly. Similarly, when you run on H1, it may not load M1 data, it could also mean missing the appropriate HST files. Because of that, EA got conditions to check for the valid available data, before running the strategies. So the optimal way is to run on M15 or M30, then all timeframes between M1 and M30 data should be available. If still won't work, there is something missing in your configuration. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

It's with minimal lot size for good risk management and safety where DD is less than 5% (Lite/Advanced), but you can increase the lot size accordingly if you need higher risk and %. Or starting with a smaller deposit (e.g. 1000), the % can be much higher.  
Also the setup could be not optimal yet, it can be further optimized for your broker data.

I always stand for a good job and you do it well. keep it up !! . I will be watching this thread. I personally do not use any indicators. I try to manage only profit and loss. I did it, checked hundreds of indicators - in my opinion, opening positions can be completely random - it is important to then maximize profits and cut losses accordingly. you always have a 50% chance of opening a position in the right direction. it is enough that your profit will be 1 pip more than your loss, you are ahead with tens of thousands of trades. no analysis makes sense, it's just a waste of time

Sorry for the delayed reply, I had some pause for the project. I usually respond quicker on Telegram.  
  

> [Quoting mavidelisi](/thread/post/14222211#post14222211 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hello ; First of all, I would like to thank you for the robot you shared. I have been a writer for 20 years, I have not seen anyone write in this way.  
>  taking the macd, cci and moving average indicator, I would like to mention a few of my questions. Strategy actives and strategy stops. As an example here, let's assume that we have selected macd in a 5-minute strategy. In strategy stops, let's take the Moving Average in the 1-hour part.  
>  **1 - Exactly what strategy actives and strategy stops do**.
> 
> Ignored

Active strategy are responsible for market analysis and mainly for opening the trades. For closing as well, however when you set different stop strategy, you override defaults strategy with another to manage its stops (TP/SL).  
  
Let's say, you've active strategy as RSI, and stop strategy set to Bands.  
Strategy RSI relies on RSI indicator values (based on assigned timeframe), based on the signal open logic, it'll open buy at <20 value, and sell at >80 value. After open, strategy monitors its own opened trades/orders for closing signals.  
There are two ways order can be closed.  
First way is by opposite signal (buy signal will trigger closure of existing sell trades, and other way round), in case of RSI, when you hit <20 indicator value, you close active sells and so on. This type of closure is monitoring by strategy code in the background when to close.  
Second method for closing order is by stops, this is by settings TP/SL values and it's outside of strategy control when the stops are triggered. In case of RSI, based on the current implementation, strategy scans for last (let's say 12) candles where indicator values were at peak, then set trailing stops at these peak prices. In case of other indicators which produces prices as output (not range values such as 0-100), the stops are set by its peak indicator values.  
  
So when you set Bands strategy to manage stops, then the order is opened by signals based on RSI values, logic for closing order on opposite signal is also RSI, you're just override updating of TP/SL values. So every candle, the trailing stops are managed by Bands strategy which are stops based on Bollinger Bands indicator values.  
For example your order is opened for buy at RSI <20, then can be closed when price upper value of Bands indicator. Basically combination of two indicators.  
  
So in your example, MACD strategy will open order when signal crosses main line in lower part of histogram in M5 timeframe, and setting MA on H1 strategy for stops, will close at peak of MA value in H1 timeframe.

  * [#443](/thread/post/14443140#post14443140 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:59am  May 31, 2023 2:39am | Edited 2:59am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting mavidelisi](/thread/post/14222211#post14222211 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 2 - In the selected strategies, if more than one strategy is selected, does it need to receive signals from all of them at the same time, or does it process signals from each of them separately?
> 
> Ignored

The idea of strategies are that they can be run independently as much as possible, so the results can be reliable and repeatable. With trading, tiny influence can change the whole result. That was the issue with v1 releases, strategies were relying too much on some shared options, and on slight change, you had to re-optimize all strategies from scratch. With v2 releases, each strategy has its own isolated parameters and logic, then assigned to specific timeframes.  
And the main EA (acts as strategy manager) [checks for each strategy](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/EA.mqh#L410-L437) for its signal (see: [SignalOpen()](https://github.com/EA31337/Strategy-RSI/blob/v1.012/Stg_RSI.mqh#L90-L113), each strategy implements its own signal) which are mainly based on indicator values attached to the given strategy.  
It's possible that multiple strategies can trigger signal (2 buys, 1 sell) after certain filters, these are processed by [signal manager](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/EA.mqh#L258-L343) (see: [TradeSignalManager.h](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/Trade/TradeSignalManager.h)) which decides whether to open trades or not. For example strategy could raise signals, but EA will reject it, because of some filters set by users (outside of peak hours, too many orders from the same strategy, one signal per candle filter, daily limit, margin used >1%, strategy's order needs to be better positioned than last time, and so on). So strategy manager has the final call whether to translate signal into actual trade. Using conditions, you can also suspend strategy from trading for certain amount of time. Each signal is like a object/struct, you can manage it, but they can be quickly expired when the price moves out of the target range. In v3 releases, signal manager receiving multiple signals at the same time would be able to prioritize based on some criteria (e.g. out of 5 signals in the same candle, pick the one from the strategy which has the highest profit factor or wins). This was part of v1 releases, but it was too complex to optimize reliably, as one small global change was breaking all other strategies, so v2 introduces more isolation between strategies (once you optimize strategy on its own, there is aim of minimal influence from the EA to change the trading logic), and v3 will add even more complex filters and rules.

  * May 31, 2023 2:48am  May 31, 2023 2:48am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting mavidelisi](/thread/post/14222211#post14222211 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 3 - How can I manually set the stoploss and takeprofit? When I put a fixed takeprofit on the robot (example 20 pips), it does not close orders when it becomes profitable by 20 pips, sometimes it takes a very short profit and sometimes it comes out the wide stop opens and closes at a loss.
> 
> Ignored

Each strategy has its own TP/SL logic implemented based on the indicator values, making it fixed, it's missing the point of isolation of different strategies, because you apply something shared across all of it. You've to write custom strategy or pick the one which implements such fixed stops (there are few I think, but I think I can write more which can do some fixed stops). To override stops for strategy, you've to override [PriceStop()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/Strategy.mqh#L1004).  
There is still a way to set maximum SL/TP in pips, check 'Close loss/profit (in pips)' params in EA Advanced (as Lite is designed to run strategies as they are in pure/isolated form, and aim of Rider is to have closure based on equity conditions, not fixed values). This won't change the logic of strategy's dynamic stops, it's just overriding the maximum stop loss that order can take in pips.

  * [#446](/thread/post/14443191#post14443191 "Post Permalink")

  * May 31, 2023 3:21am  May 31, 2023 3:21am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting mavidelisi](/thread/post/14222211#post14222211 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 4 - include/common/mode.h activated file as follows. Because I wanted to see and change the input parameters in some indicators. Only when I activate the __config__ parameter, the robot does not compile,the compiler is giving an error. i want to take the parameters from the config file I defined manually and run the robot, but when I activate the __config__ parameter, the program is not compiled.
> 
> Ignored

The __config__ option was implemented, so each instance of strategy loads with different set of parameters (like loading settings from the config file). This is the result of limitation of MetaTrader platform where you can have limited type and amount of parameters. Using select list (based on enums) and textfields for input params for EA is really too limited. The goal was to set different param values for strategy per each timeframe.  
Basically each strategy (such as [RSI](https://github.com/EA31337/Strategy-RSI/blob/v1.012/Stg_RSI.mqh#L8-L28)) comes with around 20 input parameters, with 50 strategies you've 1000 input parameters. So different settings per timeframe (~20) is around 20000 parameters for EA, which is not possible to expose to the user (btw. there is hardcoded +1100 max params or something forced by platform). So __config__ was storing different strategy's param per timeframe in [config/*.h](https://github.com/EA31337/Strategy-RSI/tree/v1.012/config) files. Then I had automated optimization tests triggered by _GitHub Actions_ which were looking for the best param values for the given timeframe and adding these values into these config files (e.g. M15.h). The thing is, once params are loaded from these config file (.h), main user's params needs to be overridden. So if you set __config__, param values from config files are overriding these set in user's inputs.  
This was an idea, but too complex to manage with 50 strategies, 10 timeframes, potentially 10 different pairs each, plus to run extensive tests, I'll have to pay for the self-runners (hard to setup due to platform limitations and issues), as these tests were too heavy for GitHub public workers to handle (secondly, they're not allowing it). At the end, I've found that is no much benefit of changing different values per timeframe per strategy. What I did, that you can still override them in EA Advanced, but still for all of them. In addition, I've hit some MQL code syntax limitations (it's not C++ at the end). So I'll have to reintroduce these individual set of params per strategy and timeframe at different way. In summary, I'm going to drop the support for this __config__ feature, so compilation errors may happen, as the code become outdated.

The same when I've tried machine learning, it learnt EURUSD, and same learning didn't apply for other pairs.

  * [#449](/thread/post/14443232#post14443232 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 7:28am  May 31, 2023 4:13am | Edited 7:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar289620_1.gif) kenorb](kenorb)

  * | Joined Sep 2012  | Status: Trader | [192 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=289620)

> [Quoting mavidelisi](/thread/post/14222211#post14222211 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> 6 - On some indicators I see the following parameters. What are these parameters, what are they useful for ? Can you explain ?  
>    
>  -Platform Built-in  
>  -Chart Calculation  
>  -iCustom : Custom indicator file  
>  -iCustom : Custom, legacy, provided by MT indicator file  
>  -OnIndicator : Another indicator as source of data  
>  -OnCalculate : Custom calculation function  
>  -MAth-based indicator
> 
> Ignored

These are sources of input data for analysis (data feeders). Not all strategies are implementing each, it depends on the indicator and platform.  
  
\- Platform Built-in  
  
This mode uses built-in mode such as documented at <https://www.mql5.com/en/docs/indicators> (e.g. iMA, iRSI).  
The values are provided by the platform and you don't have much control over the data that is provided.  
You're limited to only these which are implemented by the platform, plus different indicators are available for MT4 vs MT5, and there are different implementations between different platforms (e.g. iEnvelopes in MQL4 got 3 modes, in MQL5 there are 2), so when you're writing universal code which works for both, you've to write a lot of hacks (to provide backward compatibility).  
  
\- Chart Calculation  
  
This takes custom chart data as input. Normally you rely on OHLC from platform's chart, using this mode, you can override chart data with different one.  
Good example is [Heiken Ashi indicator](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/Indicators/Indi_HeikenAshi.mqh) which "produces" chart (it outputs OHLC). So you can run indicator on top of Heiken Ashi indicator as it would be a chart.  
Or implement your own chart, such as Renki (which is not supported by platform by default without extensive workarounds and hacks).  
  
\- iCustom : Custom indicator file  
  
The data is fed by iCustom() pointing to external indicator. Let's say I've custom implementation of iRSI which I want to use as indicator data provider, and I don't want to use Built-in (due to some limitations or bugs).  
  
\- iCustom : Custom, legacy, provided by MT indicator file  
  
In this mode, data is fed by iCustom() pointing to the indicators provided by the platform (in MT5 you can find them in Indicators/Examples). These implementations can depends on the platform versions, sometimes they patch or change something, sometimes implementation of source code is different to the one provided by builtin indicators. By switching between this and built-in mode, you can compare the differences between these implementations.  
  
\- OnIndicator : Another indicator as source of data  
  
This is something unique I guess, I didn't see this idea anywhere implemented.  
The closest way to achieve by coding, was in MQL4 (e.g. iBandsOnArray, iRSIOnArray), but dropped in MQL5.  
So it's all custom built.  
Basically you take data of one indicator, and feed into another one to calculate it.  
For example, you can calculate RSI given MA values.  
Using EA framework, this can take ideas on another level, by chaining multiple indicators, e.g. MA->RSI->Bands.  
Why? This opens possibilities to write even more sophisticated indicators and strategies which were not possible before.  
Let's say you've RSI values and normally you've to write fixed conditions such as buy at <20 (this is what most of simple strategies does).  
When you add another indicator on top of RSI, you can actually detect its pace, speed or gradual turn in opposite direction to do some trading conditions around it.  
  
\- OnCalculate : Custom calculation function  
  
Value of indicator is calculated internally by the function, check example at [MA::Calculate()](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-classes/blob/v2.012.2/Indicators/Indi_MA.mqh#L577-L606).  
This is alternative if you don't want to use iCustom() (platform builtin calls are slow, especially for indicators).  
Or you're not using platform where there is no builtin or iCustom(), such as C++/wasm implementation (available soon).  
  
\- Math-based indicator  
  
It's pure calculation of indicator values from the function. It's similar to OnCalculate(), but using different approach, this idea still not fully implemented.  
It's more useful for running/testing strategies outside of platform.

New [EA releases](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases):  
\- EA31337 v2.012.1 (Lite/Advanced/Rider) ([download](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/tag/v2.012.1)) ([results](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/discussions/355)) ([wiki](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki))  
\- EA31337 Libre v1.012 ([download](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337-Libre/releases/tag/v1.012)) (for education purposes only)  
  
## Usage  
  
\- Default settings are suitable for EURUSD pair only with spread 10 points or less.  
\- Read more at [Wiki pages](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki).  
  
## Backtests (MT5)  
  
Backtest

  1. Symbol: EURUSD

## Which version to use?  
  
Lite, Advanced and Rider have slightly different logic (despite sharing the same codebase).  
\- Lite configuration is easy to use with simple strategy configuration per timeframe, but less customizable.  
\- Advanced has more options to offer (more complex filters), ideally for advanced users.  
\- Rider is the riskiest of all as it tries to keep the orders open for longer by "riding" on the equity (which means it closes trades when EA's equity reaches certain %). Better deals with higher [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide").  
  
Which version to use, it's to you. Check [Input parameters](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki/Input-parameters) wiki page for more details.  
For MetaTrader 4, please download file with `.ex4` extension, for MetaTrader 5 use `.ex5` accordingly.  
  
**Note: For .ex4 (MT4), you've to[download from GitHub](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/releases/tag/v2.012.1), as the files are too big to upload it here (limit of 5MB).**

SignalOpenMethod  
Signal open/close methods (SOM/SCM) are type of params to control method/logic when opening or closing order. Non-zero value is used as additional filter to activate extra conditioning. It's using bitwise operation, so during optimization, all combinations can be tested.  
To explain bitwise operations, let's start with basics: ["int" type in platform is 32-bit](https://www.mql5.com/en/docs/basis/types/integer) (4 bytes), which means "int" type can store 32 different combinations (conditions in our case).  
So let's say you've base condition (in RSI, buy when <20 and sell when >80).  
Then you add multiple conditions on top of your base condition, e.g.  
if (1st-bit-of-int-is-active) _result &= TRADING_CONDITION1; // 1  
if (2nd-bit-of-int-is-active) _result &= TRADING_CONDITION2; // 2  
if (3rd-bit-of-int-is-active) _result &= TRADING_CONDITION3; // 4  
if (4th-bit-of-int-is-active) _result &= TRADING_CONDITION4; // 8  
...  
Then if you optimize SOM param between 0 and 15, you've tested all the combinations/permutations of above conditions (0+1, 0+2, 0+1+2, 0+4, 0+1+4, ...).  
This way you can write some conditions for your strategy and test out which combinations works the best.  
  
SignalOpenLevel  
Signal open/close level params (SOL/SCL) are type of param to control sensitivity of opening or closing order. The logic can vary depending if it can be used with associated indicator or not. For RSI, level 20 is calculated from the middle (50-20 vs 50+20). In MACD (in the recent version), it's percentage of change value, so you can filter out slow vs sudden movements of the indicator. For other strategies (which uses price indicators), level is additional difference between actual signal and when it's actually opened (calculated in pips) which acts like a delay or additional confirmation. Logic can vary depends on strategy. These are provided for strategy, so they can implement how it's suitable for the particular use case.  
  
SignalOpenFilterMethod/SignalCloseFilterMethod  
Same idea as above, using bitwise operations, you can test different filters. Here are the examples (this can change between versions):  
  
\- 0 - disabled  
\- 1 - avoid opening multiple trades in the same strategy's candle  
\- 2 - open trades only with the main trend  
\- 4 - open trades when price is above pivot point of the current strategy's candle  
\- 8 - do not open trades when there are opposite active trades (hedging)  
\- 16 - open trades only on candle's peak prices  
\- 32 - do not open trades when there are better one already opened in the same direction  
\- 64 - do not open trades when account's equity is lower than 1% (this option may change)  
\- -64 - do not open trades when account's equity is higher than 1% (this option may change)  
\- Note: When combining filters by a sum, AND operation applies. Negative values will negate filter.  
  
So to apply multiple filters, you just sum them together, so 24 means 8+16 filters are activated.  
Same when closing the order.  
  
OpenFilterTime  
It's using bitwise operation to filter by trading time. Same rules apply (sum activates multiple options):  
  
\- 0 - disabled  
\- 1 - Chicago's trading hours (14-23 GMT)  
\- 2 - Frankfurt's trading hours (7-16 GMT)  
\- 4 - Hong Kong's trading hours (1-10 GMT)  
\- 8 - London's trading hours (8-17 GMT)  
\- 16 - New York's trading hours (13-22 GMT)  
\- 32 - Sydney's trading hours (22-7 GMT)  
\- 64 - Tokyo's trading hours (0-9 GMT)  
\- 128 - Wellington's trading hours (22-6 GMT)  
\- Note: When combining filters by a sum, OR operation applies. Negative values will negate filter.  
  
SignalOpenBoostMethod  
Not fully implemented yet, it's going to boost lot sizes based on bitwise conditions. E.g. increase lot size by 10% if e.g. requested trade is with main trend.  
  
PriceStopMethod  
It's changing strategy's stop method by adding extra code based on bitwise operations. E.g. you can control whether your trailing stop is locked or not, or adding filter to apply additional logic. This feature is still in progress.  
  
Input parameters (including above filters) used by EA are documented in more details at this [wiki page](https://github.com/EA31337/EA31337/wiki/Input-parameters).
